## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form for (possibly driven/damped) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Typical relationships combine a restoring force term in x (often nonlinear), damping in v (often nonlinear), and optional explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (conservative small-amplitude motion)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized damped oscillator)
- Constant/linear bias force: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (gravity offset, actuator bias)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 (common nonlinear spring with losses)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (loss increasing with displacement)
- Quadratic/drag-like damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-style dissipation)
- Van der Pol-type self-excitation: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (limit-cycle oscillator with negative damping at small |x|)
- Rayleigh-type self-excitation: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (velocity-dependent negative/positive damping balance)
- Externally driven oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic forcing/drive)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/bistability under forcing)
- Parametrically modulated stiffness: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Non-smooth/frictional damping surrogate: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (Coulomb-like friction with smooth sign approximation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends on x only (no v, no t), often expressible as dv_dt = -dU/dx with U even in x for symmetric springs.
- Symmetric restoring force: for symmetric potentials, restoring terms are odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3), implying dv_dt(x) changes sign with x.
- Dissipation signature: terms proportional to v (or v*Abs(v)) remove energy; identifying dv_dt containing -c*v (or -c*v*Abs(v)) indicates damping.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of nonlinear stiffness (x**3, x**5) typically produces frequency that shifts with oscillation amplitude.
- Limit-cycle (self-oscillation) indicator: a damping coefficient that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 - c1*x**2)*v or (c0 - c1*v**2)*v, suggests stable periodic motion.
- External periodic drive: additive sin/cos terms in t indicate forced response, resonance peaks, and potential entrainment/phase-locking.
- Parametric excitation: time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (or v) indicate Mathieu-like instability tongues and parametric resonance near 2× natural frequency.
- Non-smooth dissipation: tanh(c*v), sign(v), or v*Abs(v) structures reflect dry friction or quadratic drag, producing sharper waveform peaks and faster decay at higher speeds.

- `-1.92728910930903*x*0.0682163475684738*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 1.92728910930903*x`

- `v*x²` term: `+0.424310587218182*v*x**2`
- `x` term: `-1.92728910930903*x - 1.92728910930903*x = -3.85457821861806*x`

- `sin(t)` term: `+0.30645527626767*sin(t)`

where A, B, C, D, E are specific constants.

The key basis functions are:

2. `sin(t)` 
3. `v` (linear in v)

- Candidates with `(c+v)**c*x` could potentially work if the base handles negative v appropriately, but generally `(c+v)**c` ≠ `Abs(v)**c`.

Let me systematically check:

**Candidates 1-15:** These contain terms like `v**c*x`. Since v takes both signs and `v**0.333` ≠ `Abs(v)**0.333` for negative v, these cannot match.

**Candidates 12-13, 30-33:** Have `(c+v)**c*x` — setting the constant shift to 0 gives `v**c*x`, same problem.

**Candidates 16-24, 25-29, 34-50:** Various structures — need to check for `Abs(v)` terms.

None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)` explicitly. The GT requires `Abs(v)**0.333*x`, which is fundamentally different from `v**0.333*x` when v is negative. Since v takes both positive and negative values per the domain constraints, no candidate with `v**c` can match `Abs(v)**c`.

Let me verify: Could any candidate's structure somehow produce `Abs(v)**0.333`? Terms like `log`, `sqrt`, polynomial powers — none produce absolute value behavior.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce the `Abs(v)^(1/3)*x` term required by the GT, because none use `Abs(v)` and v takes both signs.
